2025-01-13T19:14:29.6000971Z     @set_module('numpy')
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6001134Z     def load(file, mmap_mode=None, allow_pickle=False, fix_imports=True,
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6001291Z              encoding='ASCII', *, max_header_size=format._MAX_HEADER_SIZE):
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6001360Z         """
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6001541Z         Load arrays or pickled objects from ``.npy``, ``.npz`` or pickled files.
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6001612Z     
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6001809Z         .. warning:: Loading files that contain object arrays uses the ``pickle``
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6001954Z                      module, which is not secure against erroneous or maliciously
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6002113Z                      constructed data. Consider passing ``allow_pickle=False`` to
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6002261Z                      load data that is known not to contain object arrays for the
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6002367Z                      safer handling of untrusted sources.
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6002439Z     
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6002514Z         Parameters
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6002592Z         ----------
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6002712Z         file : file-like object, string, or pathlib.Path
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6002848Z             The file to read. File-like objects must support the
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6002957Z             ``seek()`` and ``read()`` methods and must always
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6003104Z             be opened in binary mode.  Pickled files require that the
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6003251Z             file-like object support the ``readline()`` method as well.
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6003369Z         mmap_mode : {None, 'r+', 'r', 'w+', 'c'}, optional
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6003522Z             If not None, then memory-map the file, using the given mode (see
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6003782Z             `numpy.memmap` for a detailed description of the modes).  A
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6003952Z             memory-mapped array is kept on disk. However, it can be accessed
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6004113Z             and sliced like any ndarray.  Memory mapping is especially useful
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6004449Z             for accessing small fragments of large files without reading the
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6004539Z             entire file into memory.
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6004635Z         allow_pickle : bool, optional
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6004809Z             Allow loading pickled object arrays stored in npy files. Reasons for
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6004989Z             disallowing pickles include security, as loading pickled data can
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6005156Z             execute arbitrary code. If pickles are disallowed, loading object
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6005255Z             arrays will fail. Default: False
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6005323Z     
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6005427Z             .. versionchanged:: 1.16.3
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6005553Z                 Made default False in response to CVE-2019-6446.
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6005620Z     
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6005709Z         fix_imports : bool, optional
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6005900Z             Only useful when loading Python 2 generated pickled files on Python 3,
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6006098Z             which includes npy/npz files containing object arrays. If `fix_imports`
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6006266Z             is True, pickle will try to map the old Python 2 names to the new names
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6006352Z             used in Python 3.
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6006436Z         encoding : str, optional
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6006726Z             What encoding to use when reading Python 2 strings. Only useful when
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6006902Z             loading Python 2 generated pickled files in Python 3, which includes
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6007077Z             npy/npz files containing object arrays. Values other than 'latin1',
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6007238Z             'ASCII', and 'bytes' are not allowed, as they can corrupt numerical
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6007321Z             data. Default: 'ASCII'
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6007416Z         max_header_size : int, optional
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6007579Z             Maximum allowed size of the header.  Large headers may not be safe
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6007749Z             to load securely and thus require explicitly passing a larger value.
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6007866Z             See :py:func:`ast.literal_eval()` for details.
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6008031Z             This option is ignored when `allow_pickle` is passed.  In that case
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6008183Z             the file is by definition trusted and the limit is unnecessary.
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6008257Z     
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6008327Z         Returns
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6008403Z         -------
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6008497Z         result : array, tuple, dict, etc.
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6008655Z             Data stored in the file. For ``.npz`` files, the returned instance
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6008823Z             of NpzFile class must be closed to avoid leaking file descriptors.
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6008891Z

2025-01-13T19:14:29.6010043Z             if all data has already been read
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6010110Z     
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6010302Z         See Also
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6010376Z         --------
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6010482Z         save, savez, savez_compressed, loadtxt
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6010652Z         memmap : Create a memory-map to an array stored in a file on disk.
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6010827Z         lib.format.open_memmap : Create or load a memory-mapped ``.npy`` file.
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6010898Z     
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6010965Z         Notes
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6011039Z         -----
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6011194Z         - If the file contains pickle data, then whatever object is stored
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6011286Z           in the pickle is returned.
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6011428Z         - If the file is a ``.npy`` file, then a single array is returned.
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6011570Z         - If the file is a ``.npz`` file, then a dictionary-like object is
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6011740Z           returned, containing ``{filename: array}`` key-value pairs, one for
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6011829Z           each file in the archive.
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6011975Z         - If the file is a ``.npz`` file, the returned value supports the
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6012156Z           context manager protocol in a similar fashion to the open function::
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6012228Z     
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6012314Z             with load('foo.npz') as data:
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6012396Z                 a = data['a']
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6012462Z     
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6012632Z           The underlying file descriptor is closed when exiting the 'with'
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6012698Z           block.
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6012767Z     
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6012841Z         Examples
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6012916Z         --------
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6013108Z         Store data to disk, and load it again:
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6013176Z     
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6013298Z         >>> np.save('/tmp/123', np.array([[1, 2, 3], [4, 5, 6]]))
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6013381Z         >>> np.load('/tmp/123.npy')
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6013461Z         array([[1, 2, 3],
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6013536Z                [4, 5, 6]])
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6013607Z     
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6013727Z         Store compressed data to disk, and load it again:
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6013801Z     
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6013885Z         >>> a=np.array([[1, 2, 3], [4, 5, 6]])
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6013969Z         >>> b=np.array([1, 2])
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6014060Z         >>> np.savez('/tmp/123.npz', a=a, b=b)
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6014155Z         >>> data = np.load('/tmp/123.npz')
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6014385Z         >>> data['a']
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6014474Z         array([[1, 2, 3],
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6014545Z                [4, 5, 6]])
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6014621Z         >>> data['b']
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6014703Z         array([1, 2])
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6014779Z         >>> data.close()
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6014851Z     
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6014989Z         Mem-map the stored array, and then access the second row
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6015073Z         directly from disk:
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6015144Z

2025-01-13T19:14:29.6015664Z         if encoding not in ('ASCII', 'latin1', 'bytes'):
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6015812Z             # The 'encoding' value for pickle also affects what encoding
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6015941Z             # the serialized binary data of NumPy arrays is loaded
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6016083Z             # in. Pickle does not pass on the encoding information to
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6016223Z             # NumPy. The unpickling code in numpy.core.multiarray is
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6016371Z             # written to assume that unicode data appearing where binary
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6016516Z             # should be is in 'latin1'. 'bytes' is also safe, as is 'ASCII'.
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6016584Z             #
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6016848Z             # Other encoding values can corrupt binary data, and we
2025-01-13T19:14:29.6017001Z             # purposefully disallow them. For the same reason, the errors=
